There will always be people whom we cannot help. In this case not only were you not able to help the other person, you also did not help yourself as you were hurt by the man’s response. When this happens, we need to develop compassion for the other person based on an understanding of how difficult it is to help sentient beings. Instead of becoming depressed, you should use that direct experience of how difficult it is to help others to become happy that you have gained such an important understanding and use it as an aid to strengthening your wish to help others.  Thursday afternoon, 13 October 2005  Necklace for Those of Clear Awareness says:  [E13] Lethargy (rmugs pa) Regarding lethargy, the Compendium of Knowledge says:  QUESTION: What is lethargy?  RESPONSE: It is an unserviceability of mind and is involved with ignorance. It has the function of assisting all [root] afflictions and secondary afflictions.   Just as it has been said above, it is a heaviness and an unserviceability of the body and mind and is a factor of ignorance.   Moreover, the Precious Garland (stanza 5.32ab) says:  Lethargy is a state of inactivity  Due to heaviness of body and mind.  The Explanation of the 'Treasury of Knowledge' says:   What is lethargy? It is a heaviness of the body and a heaviness of the mind. It is an unserviceability of the body and unserviceability of the mind.   
Basic Program: Commentary to Mind and Cognition by Geshe Tenzin Tenphel – 10-14 October 2005 (05)  
176 The Great Exposition of the Stages of the Path a l s o  e x p l a i n s  i t  i n  t h i s  w a y .  I t s  f u n c t i o n  i s  specified as "assisting all [root] afflictions and secondary afflictions," because all afflictions will increase in dependence upon lethargy. In this vein, the Exhortation to the Exceptional Resolve (Adhyasayasamcodanasutra) says:  Phlegm, wind, and bile Occur to a great extent in the bodies Of those who take joy in sleep and lethargy; Their constituents are in disorder.  For those who take joy in lethargy and sleep,  Their stomachs are unclean due to a bad diet, Their bodies are heavy and their complexions unhealthy, Even their speech is slurred.  And,   Those who take joy in lethargy and sleep Are confused and their aspirations for the Dharma degenerate. The childish completely degenerate from all excellent qualities,  Their wholesomeness degenerates, and they proceed to darkness.   Lethargy is an unserviceability of mind and is included in ignorance. It is a dullness or sleepiness of the mind that affects the body and makes one feels lethargic and unmotivated to study, work, and so forth. The Necklace says that lethargy “is a heaviness and an unserviceability of the body and mind” and the Compendium of Knowledge s a y s  “ I t  h a s  t h e  f u n c t i o n  o f  a s s i s t i n g  a l l  r o o t  afflictions and secondary afflictions.” However, the latter statement is difficult to understand in that when attachment or anger arise, we are not at all lethargic, instead we are generally full of energy! Therefore, what does it mean that lethargy assists all root and secondary afflictions? That lethargy is included in ignorance is understandable since it is a lack of clarity or fogginess of the mind. But how does it assist all the afflictions? Perhaps it is because when lethargy arises, the mind becomes unclear, whereby it is then e a s i e r  f o r  o t h e r  a f f l i c t i o n s  t o  a r i s e .  H o w e v e r ,  t h a t  l e t h a r g y  assists all the afflictions can be debated because lethargy is a heavy, dull state of mind and so it is not clear how it can act to assist the arisal of attachment and anger, which are not at all lethargic. It is said that not knowing is the cause of all afflictions, so it follows that if there is knowing the afflictions will not arise.   Necklace for Those of Clear Awareness says:  [E14] Excitement (rgod pa) Regarding excitement, the Compendium of Knowledge says:  QUESTION: What is excitement?  RESPONSE: It is an unpeacefulness of mind that subsequently engages an attractive cause. It has the function of hindering calm abiding.   Just as it has been said above, it is an awareness that, upon observing the attributes of the desire realm previously experienced, mentally scatters outwards to them and engages them with craving. Regarding this, the Precious Garland (stanza 5.32cd) says:   Excitement is an  Unpeacefulness of the body and mind.   Likewise, A Discussion of the Five Aggregates also says:    QUESTION: What is excitement?  RESPONSE: It is an unpeacefulness of mind.  
Basic Program: Commentary to Mind and Cognition by Geshe Tenzin Tenphel – 10-14 October 2005 (05)  
177  Excitement is likened to a monkey that is unable to stay still because when excitement is present the mind jumps all over the place (ENGLISH TRANSLATOR: Perhaps rgod pa c o u l d  a l s o  b e  translated as “agitation.”). It functions to hinder abiding single-pointedly on an object. The Precious Garland a n d  A Discussion of the Five Aggregates b o t h  say that excitement is an unpeacefulness of mind.   Necklace for Those of Clear Awareness says:   These points are taught in the Great Exposition of the Stages of the Path:   Its object of observation is a pleasant and attractive object. Its [subjective] aspect is an unpeacefulness of the mind that i s  s c a t t e r e d  o u t w a r d ,  a n d  i t  i s  i n v o l v e d  w i t h  attachment. Thus it engages its object with the aspect of craving. It has the function of hindering the mind from abiding on an object of observation.   Excitement observes a desirable object. Its aspect is an unpeacefulness of the mind that is scattered outward (ENGLISH TRANSLATOR: The mind goes outward – w o o s h ! ) .  F o r  e x a m p l e ,  o n e  i s  concentrating on something and suddenly the mind travels far away to something else and becomes lost in it. In this way excitement functions to hinder the mind from abiding on its observed object.   Although our mind is constantly thinking, there is good thinking and bad thinking. If one is thinking about what is said in a text, that is good. However, just allowing the mind to randomly follow whatever thoughts arise is not of much benefit, although it can be pleasant. We should not allow our thinking to become excitement.  Necklace for Those of Clear Awareness says:   QUALM: Are all outward scatterings of the mind excitement? RESPONSE: I do not hold it to be so. Excitement is involved with attachment, but the mind is frequently distracted to objects by way of afflictions other than attachment; the mind even scatters to non-afflicted virtuous objects of observation. Hence, not all scatterings of the mind are excitement.  Not all outward scatterings of the mind are excitement because excitement is based on attachment whereas the mind also scatters to other objects, including virtuous objects, due to afflictions other than attachment. Thus, the mind can be distracted to an object by afflictions other than attachment. However, when pride or haughtiness arise they are accompanied by attachment, and also when anger arises there is attachment to oneself. In spite of this, there is a scattering of the mind that is not induced by attachment. In other words, the mind can drift away even though there is no anger, attachment, and so forth present.  STUDENT 1: I t  i s  u s u a l l y  s a i d  t h a t  a t t a c h m e n t  a n d  a n g e r  c a n n o t  e x i s t  a t  t h e  s a m e  t i m e  i n  o n e  mind. Therefore, when Geshe-la says that when there is anger there is also attachment to oneself does this mean that they exist in the same mind? GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: I s  i t  n o t  p o s s i b l e  t o  h a v e  a n g e r  a n d  a t t a c h m e n t  a t  t h e  s a m e  t i m e ?  They can exist at the same time. STUDENT 1: But do they exist with respect to the same object? GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: It is possible for them to exist with respect to the same object. Necklace for Those of Clear Awareness says:  [E15] Non-faith (ma dad pa) Regarding non-faith, the Compendium of Knowledge says:  QUESTION: What is non-faith?  RESPONSE: It is a non-conviction, non-clarity19, and non-wishing of the mind with respect to virtuous phenomena, and is involved with ignorance. It has the function of acting as a support for laziness.   Just as it has been said above, it is the discordant class of faith and is involved with ignorance. It is of three types:  (1) non-faith of non-conviction in actions and their results and so forth – the discordant class of the faith of conviction;  (2) non-faith of non-clarity and a mental dislike with respect to the possessors of excellent qualities, such as the Three Jewels – the discordant class of the faith of clarity; and  (3) non-faith of non-wishing and non-seeking of liberation and so forth – the discordant class of wishing faith.   It is simply to be understood that its function [is as stated above].  The three faiths are the faith of conviction, faith of clarity, and the faith of wishing. Their opposites are the non-faith of non-conviction, non-faith of non-clarity, and non-faith of non-wishing. Non-faith is the discordant class of faith, that is, it is the opposite of faith.   Necklace for Those of Clear Awareness says:  [E16] Laziness (le lo) Regarding laziness, the Compendium of Knowledge says:  QUESTION: What is laziness?                                                          19 The Tibetan text ma dad pa is emended to read ma dang ba in accordance with the commentary below, as well as in comparison with the corresponding Compendium of Knowledge passage regarding faith. 
Basic Program: Commentary to Mind and Cognition by Geshe Tenzin Tenphel – 10-14 October 2005 (05)  
180 RESPONSE: It is a non-enthusiasm of the mind engendered by the comfort of lying down, reclining on one's side, and slouching about, and is involved with ignorance. It has the function of hindering application to the class of virtue.   Just as it has been said above, it is a non-enthusiasm of the mind for virtue due to a habit of lying down and so forth. Laziness causes the entire class of virtue to degenerate. The Close Placement of Mindfulness (Saddharmasmrtyupasthana) says:   The one basis for afflictions  Is laziness. Who has it? Wherever laziness is present, All Dharma is absent.  There are three types of laziness: the laziness of procrastination, the laziness of discouragement, and the laziness of clinging to bad activities.   Necklace for Those of Clear Awareness says:  [E17] Non-conscientiousness (bag med pa) Regarding non-conscientiousness, the Compendium of Knowledge says:  QUESTION: What is non-conscientiousness?  RESPONSE: Abiding with attachment, hatred, ignorance as well as laziness, it is a non-cultivation of virtuous qualities and non-guarding of the mind against contaminated phenomena. It has the function of acting as a support for the increase of non-virtue and the decrease of virtue.   Just as it has been said above, it is an awareness that, not guarding the mind against the hosts of afflictions and misdeeds, gives in to relaxation. In this regard, A Discussion of the Five Aggregates says:   QUESTION: What is non-conscientiousness?  RESPONSE: It is a non-guarding of the mind against afflictions due to attachment, hatred, ignorance, or laziness, and is a non-cultivation of virtue.  It is simply to be understood that its function [is as stated above].  Non-conscientiousness is a lack of care regarding what one does.   Necklace for Those of Clear Awareness says:  [E18] Forgetfulness (brjed nges pa) Regarding forgetfulness, the Compendium of Knowledge says:  QUESTION: What is forgetfulness?  RESPONSE: It is a mindfulness that is concomitant with afflictions. It has the function of acting as a support for distraction.   Just as it has been said above, it is a knower that is an unclear mind and forgetful with respect to virtue on account of mindfulness of an object of observation of afflictions. Similarly, A Discussion of the Five Aggregates also explains forgetfulness to be an afflicted mindfulness, whereby an unclear, forgetful, virtuous mind should be called "forgetfulness." However, since the objects of observation of afflictions – pleasant and unpleasant characteristics and so forth – do not arise as objects of awareness[of such a virtuous mind], perhaps it should not be posited as forgetfulness. Forgetfulness acts as a support for distraction, because, in dependence on afflicted mindfulness, the mind will be distracted to an object of observation of the afflictions. 
Basic Program: Commentary to Mind and Cognition by Geshe Tenzin Tenphel – 10-14 October 2005 (05)  
181  Forgetfulness is afflicted mindfulness. Due to being mindful of an afflicted object, the mindfulness of a virtuous object decreases. Mindfulness or memory functions to hold something in the mind, but this does not happen without effort. In other words, it is necessary to train in and cultivate mindfulness until one becomes able to hold what one reads, hears, and so forth in the mind. Forgetfulness is distracted to an afflicted object.  Necklace for Those of Clear Awareness says:  [E19] Non-introspection (shes bzhin ma yin pa) Regarding non-introspection, the Compendium of Knowledge says:  QUESTION: What is non-introspection?  RESPONSE: It is a wisdom that i s  c o n c o m i t a n t  w i t h  a f f l i c t i o n s  a n d  e n g a g e s  unknowingly in activities of body, speech, and mind. It has the function of acting as a support for infractions.   Just as it has been said above, it is an afflicted wisdom that engages unknowingly in activities of the three doors; it is the discordant class of introspection. That this non-introspection acts as a support for infractions accords with what is said in Engaging in the Bodhisattva Deeds (stanza 5.26):   Even though learned,  Faithful and diligent in effort,  Many become tainted by downfalls  Due to the fault of lacking introspection.   (ENGLISH TRANSLATOR: Shes bzhin ma yin pa could be better translated as “non-awareness.”) Introspection is knowing what one is doing while o n e  i s  d o i n g  i t .  T h u s ,  n o n-introspection is an afflicted wisdom that engages while unknowing in activities of the three doors. Introspection knows what is present in the mind, for example, lethargy or excitement, whereas non-introspection does not know this. Mindfulness is a non-forgetting, it does not forget what has been learned and studied, what is right and wrong, and so forth. Mindfulness and introspection work together, but they have different functions.  STUDENT: W h y  i s  n o n-introspection mentioned among the secondary mental afflictions, but introspection, which is so important, is not included among the mental factors? GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: S o me t i me s  t h i n g s  a r e  e x p l a i n e d  b y  e x p l a i n i n g  t h e i r  o p p o s i t e s .  I t  i s  true that the positive side, introspection, is not explained, but by understanding non-introspection one can understand introspection. STUDENT: So introspection would be a virtuous mental factor? GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: It would be hard to say that introspection by itself is virtuous.  Necklace for Those of Clear Awareness says:  [E20] Distraction (rnam par g.yeng ba) Regarding distraction, the Compendium of Knowledge says:  QUESTION: What is distraction?  RESPONSE: It is a scattering of the mind and is involved with attachment, hatred, and ignorance. It has the function of hindering separation from attachment.   Just as it has been said above, it causes the mind to be distracted from its object of observation through the force of afflictions. A Discussion of the Five Aggregates explains it as a scattering of the mind to the five attributes of the desire realm.   
Basic Program: Commentary to Mind and Cognition by Geshe Tenzin Tenphel – 10-14 October 2005 (05)  
182 Distraction is similar to excitement in terms of being a scattering of the mind but the difference is that excitement is motivated by attachment, whereas distraction can be motivated by one of the three poisons – attachment, hatred, or ignorance.  STUDENT: Can we be distracted to a virtuous object? GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: Yes, we can.   Friday morning, 14 October 2005  STUDENT 2: My mind is confused and my heart is bleeding. The Buddha said that we should not believe what he taught just because he said it but always examine it first, and this is what I have always tried to do for the past fourteen years. Based on this examination, and within the limits of my intelligence, I have ascertained that such things as the four noble truths, the six perfections, and so forth are correct. However, now it seems that what the Buddha said only applies if one comes to the same conclusion as the Buddha and his texts. For example, every night I have dreams that are full of concepts yet I am told that there are no conceptions in dreams. Also, I have had the direct experience that anger and attachment can exist simultaneously, yet I am told that they cannot. I try to use such things as an antidote to my pride by trying to see that perhaps I am not as intelligent as I like to think that I am. However, the Dalai Lama also has the same trouble as I do. For example, he often says that if there is no scientific evidence for the existence of Mount Meru and so forth, they should be taken out of the scriptures, but then other people come along and say that he said this out of his love for sentient beings and that in reality those with higher realizations can see Mount Meru. Also the Dalai Lama says that renunciation is to not be attached to existence, he does not say “to cyclic existence” as some people say it should be interpreted. He also says that he is a normal human being who often gets angry, but then people say “He is so humble. He does not want to be considered to be an incarnation of Chenrezig.” He also says that tulkus should live like ordinary monks and not in private mansions and so forth, but then people say “But not my tulku.” Nagarjuna also said that there is no I, but then we invent the idea of a “mere I” since we cannot accept that there is no I. So what do we have to do? Do we just turn the Buddha into an idol to be worshipped on the altar without actually following his teachings? Do we want to have Dharma centers where Dharma is practiced or do we want to be like the Taliban of Afghanistan?! GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: I t  i s  a l w a y s  b e s t  t o  e x a m i n e  a n d  i n v e s t i g a t e  b e f o r e  a c c e p t i n g  anything. At the time of the Buddha there were followers of faith, the dull facultied, who based themselves on faith alone and followers of Dharma, the sharp facultied, who based themselves on logical reasoning. It is said that everything that is Dharma is based on valid cognition and is not based on mere faith. In other words, the source of all the Dharma is valid cognition. If something is not validated by a valid cognizer, it is not to be accepted. STUDENT: If one has faith in the Dalai Lama as a living buddha, should one not believe him when he says that he is just a normal human being? GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: I am not able to say why the Dalai Lama says that, but he often says that he is a simple monk and just an ordinary being. He never says that he is special. STUDENT: We should learn to live with doubt, this is part of the human condition.   Awarenesses and Knowers says: (6) Four changeable mental factors  The sixth [group of mental factors] – the four: (1) sleep,  (2) contrition,  (3) investigation, and  (4) analysis –  can become [any of the] three, virtuous, non-virtuous, or neutral, and thus are called “changeable”. This is because such change can occur due to [there being] at the time of sleep, for instance, faith or non-faith in the Three Jewels, contrition or non-contrition for virtues and sins, and so forth.  Necklace for Those of Clear Awareness says:  
Basic Program: Commentary to Mind and Cognition by Geshe Tenzin Tenphel – 10-14 October 2005 (05)  
183 [F] The four changeable mental factors (gzhan 'gyur) There are four changeable mental factors:  (1) sleep (2) regret (3) investigation  (4) analysis  [F1] Sleep (gnyid) Regarding sleep, the Compendium of Knowledge says:  QUESTION: What is sleep?  RESPONSE: It is a withdrawal of the mind in dependence upon sleep, its cause, with respect to:  • virtue, non-virtue, and the unspecified,  • the timely and the untimely,  • and the appropriate and the inappropriate,  and is involved with ignorance. It has the function of acting as a support for failing to perform actions.   Just as it has been said above, it is an awareness that causes the engagement in objects of the sense consciousness to powerlessly withdraw inwards in dependence upon its causes, such as heaviness of body, weakness, fatigue, and attention to signs of darkness.   Here, regarding "the timely and the untimely" [in the citation above], it is just as it has been said by the Protector Nagarjuna [in his Letter to a Friend] (stanza 39):    Sensible ones! Occupy yourselves the entire daytime and  Also the first and last parts of the night.  Sleep with mindfulness between these; Then even the time of sleep will not be wasted.   Just as it has been said above, the middle watch of the night is the time for sleep, whereas the first and the last watches of the night, as well as daytime, not being the time for sleep, are times for making effort in the application of virtue. Hence it is taught in this way for the purpose of comprehending these modes.   Regarding "the appropriate and the inappropriate" [in the citation above], sleeping during the middle watch of the night out of the wish to engage in virtue by developing the elements of the body is appropriate, whereas sleep motivated by afflictions, even during the middle watch of the night, is inappropriate. Hence it is taught for the sake of understanding this. Know the reasons from the passages that have been cited above.  Its function is specified as "failing to perform actions" because, since sleep is of two types – the virtuous and the non-virtuous – t h e  n o n-virtuous type, afflicted sleep, causes virtuous activities to degenerate. That the virtuous type of sleep does exist is explained in detail in [Asanga's] Treatises on the Levels. Fearing wordiness, I have not cited the sources.  In dependence on the motivation that precedes i t ,  s l e e p  r e s p e c t i v e l y  b e c o m e s  v i r t u o u s ,  n o n-virtuous, or neutral (unspecified). This is because in itself it is neither virtuous, non-virtuous, or neutral. If an ordinary being generates a virtuous mind as he is about to fall asleep, sleep becomes virtuous. Likewise, if he generates anger when he is about to fall sleep, sleep becomes non-virtuous. If he falls asleep from within a neutral mind, sleep itself becomes neutral.   When ordinary beings dream, sometimes a dream is good and sometimes it is bad, and, when they wake up, sometimes they are remember a dream and sometimes not. It can happen that when one wakes up after having had a bad dream, that one feels unhappy and starts to worry about the reason for the bad dream. However, there is no point to worrying about this, instead one should think of the bad dream as an interference that has come to an end and thereby make one’s mind happy. In other words, one should not take a bad dream as a sign foreboding a bad event, but 
Basic Program: Commentary to Mind and Cognition by Geshe Tenzin Tenphel – 10-14 October 2005 (05)  
184 instead think of the bad dream as having eliminated an interference and feel relieved. Likewise, when we have a great dream we should not allow it to make us feel happy and special. Our minds are very fickle in that due to the slightest good experience we become extremely happy, and due to the slightest bad experience we become extremely unhappy. Instead we need to keep our mind even at all times.  STUDENT: What is neutral sleep and what result does it bring? GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: Neutral sleep just brings the short-term result of fogginess! Ha-ha!  STUDENT: What is the ripened or fruitional result of neutral sleep? GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: D i f f i c u l t  t o  s a y ,  b u t  t h e  i m m e d i a t e  r e s u l t  i s  a  k i n d  o f  s t a t e  o f  nothingness. Neutral sleep in general is state in which the mind is as though empty.  Necklace for Those of Clear Awareness says:  [F2] Regret ('gyod pa) Regarding regret, the Compendium of Knowledge says:  QUESTION: What is regret?  RESPONSE: It is a remorseful mind dependent on any [proper] activity or improper activity, intended or unintended, with respect to:  • virtue, non-virtue, and the unspecified,  • the timely and the untimely, and  • the appropriate and the inappropriate,  and is involved with ignorance. It has the function of hindering the stability of the mind.   Just as it has been said above, in dependence on: oneself having performed an appropriate or inappropriate activity deliberately or having been made to do so under duress,  being remorseful about that activity which one subsequently comes to dislike is called "generating regret."  Regret is of three types:  (1) virtuous (2) non-virtuous (3) unspecified   (1) For instance, regret for past misdeeds belongs to the class of virtue. (2) For instance, regret for having created merit belongs to the class of non-virtue.  (3) Regret for something that neither benefited nor harmed others, such as manual work, is unspecified.   "The timely and the untimely, and the appropriate and the inappropriate" [in the citation above] means that generating regret when something is rectifiable is appropriate, whereas regret when it is not is inappropriate. Moreover, appropriateness of regret when it is rectifiable refers to, for instance, the necessity to confess misdeeds with regret before the fruition has been established in the present. Not rectifiable refers to, for instance, rebirth in a bad migration due to fruition having been established; since having being born blind, physically disabled, and so forth are occasions where the fruition has been established, they are irreversible. Therefore, detailed examination of these passages from the Compendium of Knowledge seems to be a marvelous method for generating certainty regarding the stages of the path.  Also regret, another changeable mental factor, can be either virtuous, non-virtuous, or neutral. Regret is virtuous when one regrets a misdeed that has been done. Regret is non-virtuous when one regrets a meritorious action that has been done. Regret is neutral when one regrets a neutral 
Basic Program: Commentary to Mind and Cognition by Geshe Tenzin Tenphel – 10-14 October 2005 (05)  
185 action that lacks any thought of benefit or harm toward others, such as building, sewing, and so forth.   “The appropriate and the inappropriate” refers to the fact that it is necessary to regret a non-virtuous action before it ripens in its result. In other words, there is no use regretting an action after its result has already ripened. On the other hand, to regret it before it ripens is appropriate regret and timely regret. Untimely regret is to regret an action after its result has ripened.   Necklace for Those of Clear Awareness says:  [F3 & F4] Investigation (rtog pa) and analysis (dpyod pa) Regarding investigation and analysis, the Compendium of Knowledge says:  QUESTION: What is investigation?  RESPONSE: It is a mental expression of inquiry depending on either intention or wisdom; it is a coarse mind.  QUESTION: What is analysis?  RESPONSE: It is a mental expression of individual examination depending on either intention or wisdom; it is a fine mind.  Their function is to act as a support for abiding in contact and not abiding in contact.  Just as it has been said above, investigation is an inquiry into the rough entities of objects as well as their names, whereas analysis analyzes with fine discrimination.   A Discussion of the Five Aggregates also says:   QUESTION: What is investigation?  RESPONSE: It is a mental expression of inquiry. It is a coarse mind [depending on] the particularities of either intention or wisdom.  QUESTION: What is analysis?  RESPONSE: It is a mental expression of individual examination. It is a fine mind [depending on] the particularities of either intention or wisdom.  The two brothers [Asanga and Vasubandhu] seem to agree on this explanation. The function of investigation and analysis is specified as " acting as a support for abiding in contact and not abiding in contact," because investigation and analysis are each of two types – the virtuous and the non-virtuous – whereby:  investigation and analysis belonging to the class of virtue act to produce pleasant results, thus "acting as a support for abiding in contact" with happiness, and  investigation and analysis belonging to the class of non-virtue act to produce unpleasant results, thus "acting as a support for not abiding in contact" with happiness.  Moreover,  investigation and fine analysis of the meaning of selflessness with the thought to d e f i n i t e l y  emerge from cyclic existence, and so forth belong to the class of virtue,  investigation and fine analysis of the modes of pleasant or unpleasant objects motivated by attachment, anger, and so forth belong to the class of non-virtue, and  analysis and investigation of work, behavior, and so forth that are neither virtuous nor non-virtuous minds are unspecified.   The difference between investigation and analysis is that investigation is coarse while analysis is fine. Coarse examination of a virtuous object, such as examining the meaning of selflessness with 
Basic Program: Commentary to Mind and Cognition by Geshe Tenzin Tenphel – 10-14 October 2005 (05)  
186 the thought to definitely emerge from cyclic existence, is virtuous investigation, whereas the fine examination of it is virtuous analysis. When one examines an unpleasant object motivated by anger, initially there arises investigation that is non-virtuous but as one analyzes it in more detail there arises analysis that is non-virtuous. Examining a neutral action such as sewing in a coarse way is unspecified or neutral investigation, whereas if i t  i s  d o n e  m o r e  f i n e l y  i t  b e c o m e s  unspecified or neutral analysis.  The fifty-one mental factors are to be studied for the purpose of subduing the mind. This is because by studying them one comes to understand which ones are virtuous and non-virtuous and so forth. For this reason it is very useful to understand them.   STUDENT: Is this list of fifty-one mental factors exhaustive of all mental factors, or are there other mental factors that are not included in the fifty-one? GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: They are probably all included in the fifty-one. For example, in the retinue of a yogic direct perceiver there exist the five omnipresent mental factors and five object ascertaining mental factors, but what else could there be? STUDENT: There is introspection which is not included in the fifty-one. STUDENT 2: Also fear is not included in the fifty-one. GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: Perhaps fear could be included among the feelings. STUDENT 3: There are different kinds of fear, it is not always negative, for example, if someone is trying to kill me and I flee out of fear, that is not non-virtuous. On the other hand, if fear stops me from engaging in a virtuous action, then it could be non-virtuous. GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: That is right.   STUDENT: Why is generosity not included in the mental factors, whereas miserliness is? GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: It is similar to the case of non-introspection being included, but not introspection. In other words, by understanding miserliness, one can understand generosity.   Awarenesses and Knowers says: (6) Ancillarily, the mode of asserting tenets  Ancillarily, with respect to the mode of asserting tenets, the Vaibhashikas, Sautrantika Svatantrika Madhyamikas, and Prasangikas assert that direct valid cognizers are limited to three:  (1) sense direct perceivers,  (2) mental direct perceivers, and  (3) yogic direct perceivers.   This is because they do not assert self-knowing direct perceivers. The Sautrantikas, Chittamatrins, and Yogachara Svatantrika Madhyamikas assert direct valid cognizers to be limited to four:  (1) sense direct perceivers, (2) mental direct perceivers,  (3) self-knowing direct perceivers, and  (4) yogic direct perceivers.   The Sautrantikas assert that whatever is a direct perceiver is necessarily a non-mistaken consciousness, but the Chittamatrins do not, for Chittamatrins assert that a sense direct perceiver in the continuum of an ordinary person apprehending a form is a mistaken consciousness. Apply this similarly to the latter four [sense direct perceivers] – sense direct perceivers apprehending sounds and so forth. The Yogachara Svatantrika Madhyamikas have similar [assertions].  The Sautrantikas assert that whatever is a direct perceiver is necessarily a non-mistaken consciousness, for they assert that a sense direct perceiver in the continuum of an ordinary person apprehending a form is a non-mistaken consciousness. This is because they assert that a 
Basic Program: Commentary to Mind and Cognition by Geshe Tenzin Tenphel – 10-14 October 2005 (05)  
187 form is an external object in just the way that it appears to be one to a sense direct perceiver in the continuum of an ordinary person apprehending a form.  The Sautrantikas and Chittamatrins, as well as the Svatantrikas, assert that direct perceivers are necessarily free from conceptuality, but Prasangikas do not. This is because there are many differences in [the Prasangikas’] mode of assertion:  [they] assert “incontrovertible knower” to be the definition of “valid cognizer”;  that subsequent cognizers are necessarily valid cognizers;  that among direct valid cognizers there are both conceptual and non-conceptual consciousnesses;  and so forth.   According to Kay-drup’s Ocean of Reasoning, Explanation of (Dharmakirti’s) “Commentary on (Dignaga’s) ‘Compendium on Valid cognition’”: “Here [in Prasangika] the definition of ‘valid cognizer’ is ‘that which is incontrovertible.’” Such is asserted in accordance with how it is posited in the world. In the world, without distinguishing new incontrovertibility, that which is incontrovertible in general is posited as a valid cognizer and thus it is clear that even subsequent cognizers that are induced by non-conceptual direct valid cognizers are asserted as valid cognizers. Because of this there are direct valid cognizers even among conceptual valid cognizers.”  The order of the four direct perceivers must be just as it is, for Gen-dun-drup’s Ornament for Valid Reasoning: The General Meaning of (Dharmakirti’s) “Commentary on (Dignaga’s) ‘Compendium of Valid cognition’” says, “In what way is the order of the four direct perceivers definite? [Answer]: Since yogic direct perceivers exist only in the continua of Superiors, they are indicated last; since the other three [direct perceivers] exist in the continua of both common beings and Superiors, they are indicated first. Moreover, within those [first three], the two other knowers are indicated first because they are objects of experience; since self-knowers experience both of those, they are indicated last. Furthermore, between [the first two], sense direct perceivers are indicated first because they are causes [of mental direct perceivers] and mental direct perceivers are indicated last because they are effects.”  This different assertions of the four schools will be discussed in more detail when we study them during the subject of Tenets. This section can be understood just by reading it since it is quite straightforward.   Awarenesses and Knowers says: III. Expressive Sounds With respect to the third, expressive sounds, there are two parts: (1) definition and (2) divisions. 1. Definition First, the definition of something’s being an expressive sound is: an object of hearing that causes the understanding of its own object of expression through the force of nomenclature.  An expressive sound is a sound that expresses a meaning, hence it is a vocalization. “Nomenclature” is something that has the ability to identify and communicate, it can include even a gesture or a symbol, but here it refers to speech that causes understanding of its object. (ENGLISH TRANSLATOR: Expressive sounds are a division of object-possessor.) It is a sound that enables one to identify something.   Awarenesses and Knowers says: 2. Divisions 
Basic Program: Commentary to Mind and Cognition by Geshe Tenzin Tenphel – 10-14 October 2005 (05)  
188 When these are divided by way of entity, there are three:  (1) names,  (2) phrases, and  (3) letters. (1) Names With respect to the first, [names], there are two parts: (1) definition and (2) divisions. 1. Definition First, the definition of something’s being a name is: an object of hearing that causes understanding of its own meaning.  “Its own meaning” refers to its respective object, for example, hearing the word “pot” spoken causes understanding of the actual object, pot.   Awarenesses and Knowers says: 2. Divisions When these are divided, there are two: (1) actual names and  (2) designated names.   The definition of the actual name of a certain object is: that which is observed as the common locus of: 1. being a term initially applied arbitrarily to that object and 2. being the main name of that object.  The definition of the designated name of a certain object is: that which is observed as a common locus of: 3. being a term later applied to that object and  4. being a secondary name of that object.  An actual name is a term that is initially a p p l i e d  t o  a n  o b j e c t  a n d  t h a t  i s  i t s  main n a m e .  A  designated name is one that is given to an object later on and is its secondary name. However, when someone takes ordination or refuge, for example, he is given a new name. According to this definition, that name is not an actual name because the name that one was initially given is the name that one’s parents gave one when one was born. However, the ordination name can become the main name. In this case, it is neither an actual name nor a designated name. For example, in my own case I was given the name “Tenzin Tenphel” at the age of nine when I became a monk, although my parents had initially called me “Lhagpa Tsering.” Although I have been called “Tenzin Tenphel” since the age of nine, that cannot be my actual name because it is not my initial name, and it also cannot be a designated name since it is my main name. This problem is resolved by the fact that an actual name is a name that is initially applied to a particular object. Following this line of reasoning, my actual name is Tenzin Tenphel because it was initially applied to the object that had just become a monk. Thus, there is no contradiction in it being my actual name because it is the name that was initially applied to a particular object, the new monk.   STUDENT: So Tenzin Tenphel did not exist before that? GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: Tenzin Tenphel did exist before that time because there was already another Tenzin Tenphel living in Sera Je Monastery in Tibet! This is a fairly common name among Tibetans.  Awarenesses and Knowers says: 
Basic Program: Commentary to Mind and Cognition by Geshe Tenzin Tenphel – 10-14 October 2005 (05)  
189  An illustration of an actual name is speech calling the king of beasts “lion.”  When designated names are divided, there are two:  (1) names designated by reason of similarity and  (2) names designated by reason of relationship.   An illustration of the first [a name designated by reason of similarity] is speech calling a brahmin’s son who has a big mouth and pug nose “lion”; this is because Dharmakirti’s Commentary on (Dignaga’s) “Compendium on Valid cognition” s a y s ,  “ C a l l i n g  t h e  s o n  o f  a  brahman ‘lion’ in this way exists also in the world.”  With respect to the second, [names designated by reason of relationship], there are two:  (1) names designated by reason of a causal relationship and  (2) names designated by reason of a relationship of nature.   With respect to the first, [a name designated by reason of a causal relationship,] there are two:  (1) designated names in which the name of the cause is designated to the effect and  (2) designated names in which the name of the effect is designated to the cause.  An illustration of the first, [a designated name in which the name of the cause is designated to the effect,] is speech calling sunlight “sun.”   An illustration of the second, [a designated name in which the name of the effect is designated to the cause,] is speech calling a correct proof statement “an inferential cognizer.”   An illustration of the second, a name designated by reason of a relationship of nature is speech calling the burned fringe of a piece of cloth “burned cloth.”  A designated name is not the actual name of an object, it is one that is designated based on one of reasons mentioned above.   Awarenesses and Knowers says: (2) Phrases With respect to the second [of the threefold division of expressive sounds], the definition of a phrase is: an object of hearing that indicates [meaning] by joining a substratum and attribute.  An illustration [of a phrase] is “Alas, products are impermanent, subject to production and disintegration.”  (ENGLISH TRANSLATOR: A “substratum” or attribute-possessor is that which possesses the attribute or feature.)  This definition is not as straightforward as it initially seems because normally the term tshig i n  Tibetan just means “word” and can refer even to a one syllable word such as dog, cat, mouse, and so forth. It does not normally refer to a series of words. According to the definition given here, it would follow that “boy” is not a word.   Awarenesses and Knowers says: 
Basic Program: Commentary to Mind and Cognition by Geshe Tenzin Tenphel – 10-14 October 2005 (05)  
190 (3) Letters With respect to the third [of the threefold division of expressive sounds] the definition of a letter is: a vocalization that is a basis of forming the two, names and phrases.  Illustrations [of letters] are the thirty letters, ka, and so forth.  (ENGLISH TRANSLATOR: Yi ge is perhaps better translated as “syllable” rather than “letter.”) GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: Are the words on the page in front of you composed of letters? STUDENT: They are letters. GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: T h e y  a r e  n o t  l e t t e r s ,  r a t h e r  t h e y  a r e  t h e  f o r m s  o f  l e t t e r s .  A r e  t h e y  sounds? STUDENT: No. GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: That is writing, is it not? Words are sounds. Is “Edoardo” a letter? STUDENT: It is a sound when spoken. GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: It is not a sound, it is a person. According to the definition here, the form of a letter is what is written, where a letter itself is a sound. The three, names, phrases, and letters, are all expressive sounds.   Awarenesses and Knowers says:  When expressive sounds are terminologically divided, there are two: (1) sounds that express types and  (2) sounds that express collections.  With respect to the difference between sounds that express types and sounds that express collections, there are four possibilities:  (1) something that is a sound that expresses a type but not a sound that expresses a collection,  (2) something that is a sound that expresses a collection but not a sound that expresses a type,  (3) something that is both of those, and  (4) something that is neither of those.  The first possibility exists because the sound that expresses “object of knowledge” is a sound that expresses a type but is not a sound that expresses a collection. The first reason, [i.e., that the sound expressing “object of knowledge” is a sound expressing a type,] has already been established.  The sound that expresses “object of knowledge” is a sound that expresses a type but not a sound that expresses a collection.  Awarenesses and Knowers says:  The second possibility, [a sound that expresses a collection but not a sound that expresses a type,] exists because the sound that expresses “the two, pillar and pot” is a sound that expresses a collection but not a sound that expresses a type.  The sound that expresses “pillar and pot” is a sound that expresses a collection but not a sound that expresses a type because there is no phenomenon that is both a pillar and a pot.  Awarenesses and Knowers says:  The third possibility, [both a sound that expresses a collection and a sound that expresses a type,] exists because the sound expressing “pot” is both of those.  
Basic Program: Commentary to Mind and Cognition by Geshe Tenzin Tenphel – 10-14 October 2005 (05)  
191 The sound that expresses “pot” is a sound that expresses both a collection and a sound that expresses a type:  Awarenesses and Knowers says:  The fourth possibility, [something that is neither a sound that expresses a collection nor a sound that expresses a type,] exists because the sound that expresses “the two, permanent phenomenon and thing” is neither of those two.  The sound that expresses “permanent phenomenon and functioning thing” is neither a sound that expresses a collection nor a sound that expresses a type.   In brief, the sound that expresses “object of knowledge” is a sound that expresses a type because object of knowledge is a generality that includes many specifics or particulars in that all existents are objects of knowledge. Therefore, it expresses a type that is a generality. The sound that expresses “pot and pillar” is a sound that expresses a collection because both pot and pillar are matter, which is composed of a collection of particles. It is not a sound that expresses a type because there is nothing that is both pot and pillar. The sound that expresses “pot” is a sound that expresses a collection because pot is made of a collection of particles, and it is a sound that expresses a type because there are many kinds of pots, such as gold pot and so forth. The sound that expresses “permanent phenomenon and functioning thing” is not a sound that expresses a type because there is nothing that is both a permanent phenomenon and a functioning thing, and it is not a sound that expresses a collection because permanent phenomenon and functioning thing are not collections of particles in that they are not matter.   STUDENT: Therefore, the sound that expresses “mind” is not a sound that expresses a collection? GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: That is right because mind is not matter.   STUDENT: Is everything that is a “type” a generality, like object of knowledge? GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: Yes, type refers to a generality.  STUDENT: Yesterday it was said that anger and attachment can arise simultaneously because they can arise in the retinue of two different main minds that arise simultaneously. Is that right? GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: Yes, that is right: STUDENT: For example, there could be an eye consciousness that is concomitant with attachment and simultaneously a mental consciousness that is concomitant with anger? GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: I  a m  n o t  s u r e  t h a t  a t t a c h m e n t  c a n  o c c u r  i n  t h e  r e t i n u e  o f  a n e y e  consciousness. STUDENT: I f  t w o  m a i n  m i n d s  a r i s e  s i m u l t a n e o u s l y  t h e y  m u s t  b e  d i f f e r e n t ,  f o r  e x a m p l e ,  t h e r e  cannot exist two mental consciousnesses at the same time. GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: There can exist two mental consciousnesses at the same time, but one is stronger than the other. STUDENT: So two mental consciousnesses can arise simultaneously? GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: Yes, of course. STUDENT: I  w a s  t h i n k i n g  t h a t  t h e y  c o u l d  n o t .  T h e r e f o r e ,  a n g e r  a n d  a t t a c h m e n t  c a n  a r i s e  simultaneously because they arise simultaneously in the retinue of two different main minds? GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: That is right.  STUDENT: Geshe-la said previously that a contradiction is not its parts and that it is not itself, but yet it still exists. To me this means that it exists independently. So could Geshe-la please give another example of something that is not its parts and not itself (the collection of its parts)? GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: A contradiction is not its parts and is not its collection of parts, but it still exists in dependence on its parts. STUDENT: Then Geshe-la is not his parts nor his collection of its parts, but he exists in dependence on his parts.  GESHE TENZIN TENPHEL: A contradiction is not a contradiction, for example, permanent and impermanent.
